Chapter 2 -- The Clan Rose scramble into the china-closet as rapidly a possible , and there refresh herself by make face at Debby , while she settle her plumage and screw up her courage .
Then she creep softly down the hall and peep into the parlor .
No one appear , and all be so still she felt sure the company be upstairs .
So she skip boldly through the half-open folding-doors , to behold on the other side a sight that nearly take her breath away .
Seven boys stand in a row all age , all size , all yellow-haired and blue-eyed , all in full Scotch costume , and all smiling , nodding , and say a with one voice , `` How be you , cousin ? ''
Rose give a little gasp , and look wildly about her a if ready to fly , for fear magnify the seven and the room seem full of boy .
Before she could run , however , the tall lad step out of the line , say pleasantly , `` Do n't be frighten .
This be the Clan come to welcome you ; and I 'm the chief , Archie , at your service . ''
He hold out his hand a he speak , and Rose timidly put her own into a brown paw , which close over the white morsel and hold it a the chief continue his introduction .
`` We come in full rig , for we always turn out in style on grand occasion .
Hope you like it .
Now I 'll tell you who these chap be , and then we shall be all right .
This big one be Prince Charlie , Aunt Clara 's boy .
She have but one , so he be an extra good one .
This old fellow be Mac , the bookworm , call Worm for short .
This sweet creature be Steve the Dandy .
Look at his glove and top-knot , if you please .
They be Aunt Jane 's lad , and a precious pair you 'd better believe .
These be the Brats , my brother , Geordie and Will , and Jamie the Baby .
Now , my men , step out and show your manner . ''
At this command , to Rose 's great dismay , six more hand be offer , and it be evident that she be expect to shake them all .
It be a try moment to the bashful child ; but , remember that they be her kinsman come to welcome her , she try her best to return the greeting cordially .
This impressive ceremony be over , the Clan break rank , and both room instantly appear to be pervade with boy .
Rose hastily retire to the shelter of a big chair and sit there watch the invader and wonder when her aunt would come and rescue her .
As if bound to do their duty manfully , yet rather oppress by it , each lad pause beside her chair in his wandering , make a brief remark , receive a still briefer answer , and then sheer off with a relieved expression .
Archie come first , and , lean over the chair-back , observe in a paternal tone , `` I 'm glad you 've come , cousin , and I hope you 'll find the Aunt-hill pretty jolly . ''
`` I think I shall . ''
Mac shake his hair out of his eye , stumble over a stool , and ask abruptly , `` Did you bring any book with you ? ''
`` Four box full .
They be in the library . ''
Mac vanish from the room , and Steve , strike an attitude which display his costume effectively , say with an affable smile , `` We be sorry not to see you last Wednesday .
I hope your cold be well . ''
`` Yes , thank you . ''
And a smile begin to dimple about Rose 's mouth , a she remember her retreat under the bed-cover .
Feeling that he have be receive with distinguished mark of attention , Steve stroll away with his topknot higher than ever , and Prince Charlie prance across the room , say in a free and easy tone , `` Mamma send her love and hop you will be well enough to come over for a day next week .
It must be desperately dull here for a little thing like you . ''
`` I 'm thirteen and a half , though I do look small , '' cry Rose , forget her shyness in indignation at this insult to her newly acquire teen .
`` Beg pardon , ma'am ; never should have guess it . ''
And Charlie go off with a laugh , glad to have strike a spark out of his meek cousin .
Geordie and Will come together , two sturdy eleven and twelve year olders , and , fix their round blue eye on Rose , fire off a question apiece , a if it be a shooting match and she the target .
`` Did you bring your monkey ? ''
`` No ; he be dead . ''
`` Are you go to have a boat ? ''
`` I hope not . ''
Here the two , with a right-about-face movement , abruptly march away , and little Jamie demand with childish frankness , `` Did you bring me anything nice ? ''
`` Yes , lot of candy , '' answer Rose , whereupon Jamie ascend into her lap with a sound kiss and the announcement that he like her very much .
This proceeding rather startle Rose , for the other lad look and laugh , and in her confusion she say hastily to the young usurper , `` Did you see the circus go by ? ''
`` When ?
Where ? ''
cry all the boy in great excitement at once .
`` Just before you come .
At least I think it be a circus , for I saw a red and black sort of cart and ever so many little pony , and -- '' She get no farther , for a general shout make her pause suddenly , a Archie explain the joke by say in the middle of his laugh , `` It be our new dog-cart and the Shetland pony .
You 'll never hear the last of your circus , cousin . ''
`` But there be so many , and they go so fast , and the cart be so very red , '' begin Rose , try to explain her mistake .
`` Come and see them all ! ''
cry the Prince .
And before she know what be happen , she be borne away to the barn and tumultuously introduce to three shaggy pony and the gay new dog-cart .
She have never visit these region before , and have her doubt a to the propriety of her be there now , but when she suggest that `` Auntie might not like it , '' there be a general cry of , `` She tell u to amuse you , and we can do it ever so much good out here than poke round in the house . ''
`` I 'm afraid I shall get cold without my sacque , '' begin Rose , who want to stay , but felt rather out of her element .
`` No , you wo n't !
We 'll fix you , '' cry the lad , a one clap his cap on her head , another tie a rough jacket round her neck by the sleeve , a third neatly smother her in a carriage blanket , and a fourth threw open the door of the old barouche that stand there , say with a flourish , `` Step in , ma'am , and make yourself comfortable while we show you some fun . ''
So Rose sat in state enjoy herself very much , for the lad proceed to dance a Highland Fling with a spirit and skill that make her clap her hand and laugh a she have not do for week .
`` How be that , my lassie ? ''
ask the Prince , come up all flush and breathless when the ballet be over .
`` It be splendid !
I never go to the theatre but once , and the dancing be not half so pretty a this .
What clever boys you must be ! ''
say Rose , smile upon her kinsman like a little queen upon her subject .
`` Ah , we 're a fine lot , and that be only the beginning of our lark .
We have n't get the pipe here or we 'd , ` Sing for you , play for you A dulcy melody , ' '' answer Charlie , look much elate at her praise .
`` I do not know we be Scotch ; papa never say anything about it , or seem to care about Scotland , except to have me sing the old ballad , '' say Rose , begin to feel a if she have leave America behind her somewhere .
`` Neither do we till lately .
We 've be read Scott 's novel , and all of a sudden we remember that our grandfather be a Scotchman .
So we hunt up the old story , get a bagpipe , put on our plaid , and go in , heart and soul , for the glory of the Clan .
We 've be at it some time now , and it 's great fun .
Our people like it , and I think we be a pretty canny set . ''
Archie say this from the other coach-step , where he have perch , while the rest climb up before and behind to join in the chat a they rest .
`` I 'm Fitzjames and he 's Roderick Dhu , and we 'll give you the broadsword combat some day .
It 's a great thing , you 'd better believe , '' add the Prince .
`` Yes , and you should hear Steve play the pipe .
He make 'em skirl like a good one , '' cry Will from the box , eager to air the accomplishment of his race .
`` Mac 's the fellow to hunt up the old story and tell u how to dress right , and pick out rouse bit for u to speak and sing , '' put in Geordie , say a good word for the absent Worm .
`` And what do you and Will do ? ''
ask Rose of Jamie , who sit beside her a if bound to keep her in sight till the promised gift have be hand over .
`` Oh , I 'm the little foot-page , and do errand , and Will and Geordie be the troop when we march , and the stag when we hunt , and the traitor when we want to cut any head off . ''
`` They be very obliging , I 'm sure , '' say Rose , whereat the `` utility men '' beam with modest pride and resolve to enact Wallace and Montrose as soon a possible for their cousin 's special benefit .
`` Let 's have a game of tag , '' cry the Prince , swing himself up to a beam with a sound slap on Stevie 's shoulder .
Regardless of his glove , Dandy tore after him , and the rest swarm in every direction a if bent on break their neck and dislocate their joint as rapidly a possible .
It be a new and astonishing spectacle to Rose , fresh from a prim boarding-school , and she watch the active lad with breathless interest , think their antic far superior to those of Mops , the dear depart monkey .
Will have just cover himself with glory by pitch off a high loft head first and come up all right , when Phebe appear with a cloak , hood , and rubber , also a message from Aunt Plenty that `` Miss Rose be to come in directly . ''
`` All right ; we 'll bring her ! ''
answer Archie , issue some mysterious order , which be so promptly obey that , before Rose could get out of the carriage , the boy have catch hold of the pole and rattle her out of the barn , round the oval and up to the front door with a cheer that bring two cap to an upper window , and cause Debby to cry aloud from the back porch , `` Them harum-scarum boy will certainly be the death of that delicate little creter ! ''
But the `` delicate little creter '' seem all the good for her trip , and run up the step look rosy , gay , and dishevel , to be receive with lamentation by Aunt Plenty , who beg her to go and lie down at once .
`` Oh , please do n't !
We have come to tea with our cousin , and we 'll be as good a gold if you 'll let u stay , auntie , '' clamour the boy , who not only approve of `` our cousin '' but have no mind to lose their tea , for Aunt Plenty 's name but feebly express her bountiful nature .
`` Well , dear , you can ; only be quiet , and let Rose go and take her iron and be make tidy , and then we will see what we can find for supper , '' say the old lady a she trot away , follow by a volley of direction for the approaching feast .
`` Marmalade for me , auntie . ''
`` Plenty of plum-cake , please . ''
`` Tell Debby to trot out the baked pear . ''
`` I 'm your man for lemon-pie , ma'am . ''
`` Do have fritter ; Rose will like 'em . ''
`` She 'd rather have tart , I know . ''
When Rose come down , fifteen minute later , with every curl smooth and her most beruffled apron on , she find the boy loaf about the long hall , and pause on the half-way landing to take an observation , for till now she have not really examine her new-found cousin .
There be a strong family resemblance among them , though some of the yellow head be dark than others , some of the cheek brown instead of rosy , and the age vary all the way from sixteen-year-old Archie to Jamie , who be ten year younger .
None of them be especially comely but the Prince , yet all be hearty , happy-looking lad , and Rose decide that boy be not as dreadful a she have expect to find them .
They be all so characteristically employ that she could not help smile a she look .
Archie and Charlie , evidently great crony , be pace up and down , shoulder to shoulder , whistle `` Bonnie Dundee '' ; Mac be read in a corner , with his book close to his near-sighted eye ; Dandy be arrange his hair before the oval glass in the hat-stand ; Geordie and Will investigate the internal economy of the moon-faced clock ; and Jamie lay kick up his heel on the mat at the foot of the stair , bent on demand his sweetie the instant Rose appear .
She guess his intention , and forestall his demand by drop a handful of sugar-plums down upon him .
At his cry of rapture the other lad look up and smile involuntarily , for the little kinswoman stand there above be a winsome sight with her shy , soft eye , bright hair , and laugh face .
The black frock remind them of her loss , and fill the boyish heart with a kindly desire to be good to `` our cousin , '' who have no longer any home but this .
`` There she be , as fine a you please , '' cry Steve , kiss his hand to her .
`` Come on , Missy ; tea be ready , '' add the Prince encouragingly .
`` I shall take her in . ''
And Archie offer his arm with great dignity , an honour that make Rose turn as red a a cherry and long to run upstairs again .
It be a merry supper , and the two elder boys add much to the fun by torment the rest with dark hint of some interesting event which be about to occur .
Something uncommonly fine , they declare it be , but envelop in the deep mystery for the present .
`` Did I ever see it ? ''
ask Jamie .
`` Not to remember it ; but Mac and Steve have , and like it immensely , '' answer Archie , thereby cause the two mention to neglect Debby 's delectable fritter for several minute , while they cudgel their brain .
`` Who will have it first ? ''
ask Will , with his mouth full of marmalade .
`` Aunt Plenty , I guess . ''
`` When will she have it ? ''
demand Geordie , bounce in his seat with impatience .
`` Sometime on Monday . ''
`` Heart alive !
what be the boy talk about ? ''
cry the old lady from behind the tall urn , which leave little to be see but the topmost bow of her cap .
`` Does n't auntie know ? ''
ask a chorus of voice .
`` No ; and that 's the best of the joke , for she be desperately fond of it . ''
`` What colour be it ? ''
ask Rose , join in the fun .
`` Blue and brown . ''
`` Is it good to eat ? ''
ask Jamie .
`` Some people think so , but I should n't like to try it , '' answer Charlie , laugh so he split his tea .
`` Who do it belong to ? ''
put in Steve .
Archie and the Prince star at one another rather blankly for a minute , then Archie answer with a twinkle of the eye that make Charlie explode again , `` To Grandfather Campbell . ''
This be a poser , and they give up the puzzle , though Jamie confide to Rose that he do not think he could live till Monday without know what this remarkable thing be .
Soon after tea the Clan depart , sing `` All the blue bonnet be over the border , '' at the top of their voice .
`` Well , dear , how do you like your cousin ? ''
ask Aunt Plenty , a the last pony frisk round the corner and the din die away .
`` Pretty well , ma'am ; but I like Phebe well . ''
An answer which cause Aunt Plenty to hold up her hand in despair and trot away to tell sister Peace that she never should understand that child , and it be a mercy Alec be come soon to take the responsibility off their hand .
Fatigued by the unusual exertion of the afternoon , Rose curl herself up in the sofa corner to rest and think about the great mystery , little guessing that she be to know it first of all .
Right in the middle of her meditation she fell asleep and dream she be at home again in her own little bed .
She seem to wake and see her father bending over her ; to hear him say , `` My little Rose '' ; to answer , `` Yes , papa '' ; and then to feel him take her in his arm and kiss her tenderly .
So sweet , so real be the dream , that she start up with a cry of joy to find herself in the arm of a brown , beard man , who hold her close , and whisper in a voice so like her father 's that she cling to him involuntarily , `` This be my little girl , and I be Uncle Alec . ''
Chapter 3 -- Uncles When Rose wake next morning , she be not sure whether she have dream what occur the night before , or it have actually happen .
So she hop up and dress , although it be an hour earlier than she usually rise , for she could not sleep any more , be possess with a strong desire to slip down and see if the big portmanteau and packing case be really in the hall .
She seem to remember tumble over them when she go to bed , for the aunt have send her off very punctually , because they want their pet nephew all to themselves .
The sun be shin , and Rose open her window to let in the soft May air fresh from the sea .
As she lean over her little balcony , watch an early bird get the worm , and wonder how she should like Uncle Alec , she saw a man leap the garden wall and come whistle up the path .
At first she think it be some trespasser , but a second look show her that it be her uncle return from an early dip into the sea .
She have hardly dare to look at him the night before , because whenever she try to do so she always find a pair of keen blue eye look at her .
Now she could take a good stare at him a he linger along , look about him a if glad to see the old place again .
A brown , breezy man , in a blue jacket , with no hat on the curly head , which he shake now and then like a water dog ; broad-shouldered , alert in his motion , and with a general air of strength and stability about him which please Rose , though she could not explain the feeling of comfort it give her .
She have just say to herself , with a sense of relief , `` I guess I shall like him , though he look a if he make people mind , '' when he lift his eye to examine the bud horse-chestnut overhead , and saw the eager face peer down at him .
He wave his hand to her , nod , and call out in a bluff , cheery voice , `` You be on deck early , little niece . ''
`` I get up to see if you have really come , uncle . ''
`` Did you ?
Well , come down here and make sure of it . ''
`` I 'm not allow to go out before breakfast , sir . ''
`` Oh , indeed ! ''
with a shrug .
`` Then I 'll come aboard and salute , '' he add ; and , to Rose 's great amazement , Uncle Alec go up one of the pillar of the back piazza hand over hand , step across the roof , and swung himself into her balcony , say , a he land on the wide balustrade : `` Have you any doubt about me now , ma'am ? ''
Rose be so take aback , she could only answer with a smile a she go to meet him .
`` How do my girl do this morning ? ''
he ask , take the little cold hand she give him in both his big warm one .
`` Pretty well , thank you , sir . ''
`` Ah , but it should be very well .
Why be n't it ? ''
`` I always wake up with a headache , and feel tired . ''
`` Do n't you sleep well ? ''
`` I lie awake a long time , and then I dream , and my sleep do not seem to rest me much . ''
`` What do you do all day ? ''
`` Oh , I read , and sew a little , and take nap , and sit with auntie . ''
`` No run about out of door , or house-work , or rid , hey ? ''
`` Aunt Plenty say I 'm not strong enough for much exercise .
I drive out with her sometimes , but I do n't care for it . ''
`` I 'm not surprise at that , '' say Uncle Alec , half to himself , add , in his quick way : `` Who have you have to play with ? ''
`` No one but Ariadne Blish , and she be such a goose I could n't bear her .
The boy come yesterday , and seem rather nice ; but , of course , I could n't play with them . ''
`` Why not ? ''
`` I 'm too old to play with boy . ''
`` Not a bit of it ; that 's just what you need , for you 've be molly-coddled too much .
They be good lad , and you 'll be mix up with them more or less for year to come , so you may as well be friend and playmate at once .
I will look you up some girl also , if I can find a sensible one who be not spoil by her nonsensical education . ''
`` Phebe be sensible , I 'm sure , and I like her , though I only saw her yesterday , '' cry Rose , wake up suddenly .
`` And who be Phebe , if you please ? ''
Rose eagerly tell all she know , and Uncle Alec listen , with an odd smile lurk about his mouth , though his eye be quite sober a he watch the face before him .
`` I 'm glad to see that you be not aristocratic in your taste , but I do n't quite make out why you like this young lady from the poor-house . ''
`` You may laugh at me , but I do .
I ca n't tell why , only she seem so happy and busy , and sings so beautifully , and be strong enough to scrub and sweep , and have n't any trouble to plague her , '' say Rose , make a funny jumble of reason in her effort to explain .
`` How do you know that ? ''
`` Oh , I be tell her about mine , and ask if she have any , and she say , ` No , only I 'd like to go to school , and I mean to some day . ''
`` So she do n't call desertion , poverty , and hard work , trouble ?
She 's a brave little girl , and I shall be proud to know her . ''
And Uncle Alec give an approving nod , that make Rose wish she have be the one to earn it .
`` But what be these trouble of yours , child ? ''
he ask , after a minute of silence .
`` Please do n't ask me , uncle . ''
`` Ca n't you tell them to me as well a to Phebe ? ''
Something in his tone make Rose feel that it would be good to speak out and be do with it , so she answer , with sudden colour and averted eye , `` The great one be lose dear papa . ''
As she say that , Uncle Alec 's arm come gently round her , and he draw her to him , say , in the voice so like papa 's , `` That be a trouble which I can not cure , my child ; but I shall try to make you feel it less .
What else , dear ? ''
`` I be so tired and poorly all the time , I ca n't do anything I want to , and it make me cross , '' sigh Rose , rub the ache head like a fretful child .
`` That we can cure and we will , '' say her uncle , with a decided nod that make the curl bob on his head , to that Rose saw the gray one underneath the brown .
`` Aunt Myra say I have no constitution , and never shall be strong , '' observe Rose , in a pensive tone , a if it be rather a nice thing to be an invalid .
`` Aunt Myra be a ahem !
an excellent woman , but it be her hobby to believe that everyone be totter on the brink of the grave ; and , upon my life , I believe she be offend if people do n't fall into it !
We will show her how to make constitution and turn pale-faced little ghost into rosy , hearty girl .
That 's my business , you know , '' he add , more quietly , for his sudden outburst have rather startle Rose .
`` I have forget you be a doctor .
I 'm glad of it , for I do want to be well , only I hope you wo n't give me much medicine , for I 've take quart already , and it do me no good . ''
As she speak , Rose point to a little table just inside the window , on which appear a regiment of bottle .
`` Ah , ha !
Now we 'll see what mischief these bless woman have be at . ''
And , make a long arm , Dr. Alec set the bottle on the wide railing before him , examine each carefully , smile over some , frown over others , and say , a he put down the last : `` Now I 'll show you the best way to take these mess . ''
And , as quick a a flash , he send one after another smash down into the posy-beds below .
`` But Aunt Plenty wo n't like it ; and Aunt Myra will be angry , for she send most of them ! ''
cry Rose , half frighten and half please at such energetic measure .
`` You be my patient now , and I 'll take the responsibility .
My way of give physic be evidently the best , for you look good already , '' he say , laugh so infectiously that Rose follow suit , say saucily , `` If I do n't like your medicine any good than those , I shall throw them into the garden , and then what will you do ? ''
`` When I prescribe such rubbish , I 'll give you leave to pitch it overboard as soon a you like .
Now what be the next trouble ? ''
`` I hop you would forget to ask . ''
`` But how can I help you if I do n't know them ?
Come , let u have No . 3 . ''
`` It be very wrong , I suppose , but I do sometimes wish I have not quite so many aunt .
They be all very good to me , and I want to please them ; but they be so different , I feel sort of pull to piece among them , '' say Rose , try to express the emotion of a stray chicken with six hen all clucking over it at once .
Uncle Alec throw back his head and laugh like a boy , for he could entirely understand how the good lady have each put in her oar and try to paddle her own way , to the great disturbance of the water and the entire bewilderment of poor Rose .
`` I intend to try a course of uncle now , and see how that suit your constitution .
I 'm go to have you all to myself , and no one be to give a word of advice unless I ask it .
There be no other way to keep order aboard , and I be captain of this little craft , for a time at least .
What come next ? ''
But Rose stick there , and grow so red , her uncle guess what that trouble be .
`` I do n't think I can tell this one .
It would n't be polite , and I feel pretty sure that it be n't go to be a trouble any more . ''
As she blush and stammer over these word , Dr. Alec turn his eye away to the distant sea , and say so seriously , so tenderly , that she felt every word and long remember them , `` My child , I do n't expect you to love and trust me all at once , but I do want you to believe that I shall give my whole heart to this new duty ; and if I make mistake , a I probably shall , no one will grieve over them more bitterly than I .
It be my fault that I be a stranger to you , when I want to be your best friend .
That be one of my mistake , and I never repent it more deeply than I do now .
Your father and I have a trouble once , and I think I could never forgive him ; so I keep away for year .
Thank God , we make it all up the last time I saw him , and he tell me then , that if he be force to leave her he should bequeath his little girl to me a a token of his love .
I ca n't fill his place , but I shall try to be a father to her ; and if she learn to love me half as well a she do the good one she have lose , I shall be a proud and happy man .
Will she believe this and try ? ''
Something in Uncle Alec 's face touch Rose to the heart , and when he hold out his hand with that anxious troubled look in his eye , she be move to put up her innocent lip and seal the contract with a confide kiss .
The strong arm hold her close a minute , and she felt the broad chest heave once a if with a great sigh of relief ; but not a word be speak till a tap at the door make both start .
Rose pop her head through the window to say `` come in , '' while Dr. Alec hastily rub the sleeve of his jacket across his eye and begin to whistle again .
Phebe appear with a cup of coffee .
`` Debby tell me to bring this and help you get up , '' she say , open her black eye wide , a if she wonder how on earth `` the sailor man '' get there .
`` I 'm all dress , so I do n't need any help .
I hope that be good and strong , '' add Rose , eye the steam cup with an eager look .
But she do not get it , for a brown hand take possession of it a her uncle say quickly , `` Hold hard , my lass , and let me overhaul that dose before you take it .
Do you drink all this strong coffee every morning , Rose ? ''
`` Yes , sir , and I like it .
Auntie say it ` tone ' me up , and I always feel well after it . ''
`` This account for the sleepless night , the flutter your heart get into at the least start , and this be why that cheek of yours be pale yellow instead of rosy red .
No more coffee for you , my dear , and by and by you 'll see that I be right .
Any new milk downstairs , Phebe ? ''
`` Yes , sir , plenty right in from the barn . ''
`` That 's the drink for my patient .
Go bring me a pitcherful , and another cup ; I want a draught myself .
This wo n't hurt the honeysuckle , for they have no nerve to speak of . ''
And , to Rose 's great discomfort , the coffee go after the medicine .
Dr. Alec saw the injured look she put on , but take no notice , and presently banish it by say pleasantly , `` I 've get a capital little cup among my trap , and I 'll give it to you to drink your milk in , a it be make of wood that be suppose to improve whatever be put into it something like a quassia cup .
That remind me ; one of the box Phebe want to lug upstairs last night be for you .
Knowing that I be come home to find a ready-made daughter , I pick up all sort of odd and pretty trifle along the way , hop she would be able to find something she like among them all .
Early to-morrow we 'll have a grand rummage .
Here 's our milk !
I propose the health of Miss Rose Campbell and drink it with all my heart . ''
It be impossible for Rose to pout with the prospect of a delightful boxful of gift dance before her eye ; so , in spite of herself , she smile a she drink her own health , and find that fresh milk be not a hard dose to take .
`` Now I must be off , before I be caught again with my wig in a toss , '' say Dr. Alec , prepare to descend the way he come .
`` Do you always go in and out like a cat , uncle ? ''
ask Rose , much amuse at his odd way .
`` I use to sneak out of my window when I be a boy , so I need not disturb the aunt , and now I rather like it , for it 's the short road , and it keep me limber when I have no rigging to climb .
Good-bye till breakfast . ''
And away he go down the water-spout , over the roof , and vanish among the bud honey-suckles below .
`` Ai n't he a funny guardeen ? ''
exclaim Phebe , a she go off with the cup .
`` He be a very kind one , I think , '' answer Rose , follow , to prowl round the big box and try to guess which be hers .
When her uncle appear at sound of the bell , he find her surveying with an anxious face a new dish that smoke upon the table .
`` Got a fresh trouble , Rosy ? ''
he ask , stroke her smooth head .
`` Uncle , be you go to make me eat oatmeal ? ''
ask Rose , in a tragic tone .
`` Do n't you like it ? ''
`` I de-test it ! ''
answer Rose , with all the emphasis which a turned-up nose , a shudder , and a groan could give to the three word .
`` You be not a true Scotchwoman , if you do n't like the ` parritch . '
It 's a pity , for I make it myself , and think we 'd have such a good time with all that cream to float it in .
Well , never mind . ''
And he sit down with a disappointed air .
Rose have make up her mind to be obstinate about it , because she do heartily `` detest '' the dish ; but a Uncle Alec do not attempt to make her obey , she suddenly change her mind and think she would .
`` I 'll try to eat it to please you , uncle ; but people be always say how wholesome it be , and that make me hate it , '' she say , half-ashamed at her silly excuse .
`` I do want you to like it , because I wish my girl to be as well and strong a Jessie 's boy , who be bring up on this in the good old fashion .
No hot bread and fry stuff for them , and they be the big and bonny lad of the lot .
Bless you , auntie , and good morning ! ''
Dr. Alec turn to greet the old lady , and , with a firm resolve to eat or die in the attempt , Rose sit down .
In five minute she forget what she be eat , so interested be she in the chat that go on .
It amuse her very much to hear Aunt Plenty call her forty-year-old nephew `` my dear boy '' ; and Uncle Alec be so full of lively gossip about all creation in general , and the Aunt-hill in particular , that the detested porridge vanish without a murmur .
`` You will go to church with u , I hope , Alec , if you be not too tired , '' say the old lady , when breakfast be over .
`` I come all the way from Calcutta for that express purpose , ma'am .
Only I must send the sister word of my arrival , for they do n't expect me till to-morrow , you know , and there will be a row in church if those boy see me without warn . ''
`` I 'll send Ben up the hill , and you can step over to Myra 's yourself ; it will please her , and you will have plenty of time . ''
Dr. Alec be off at once , and they saw no more of him till the old barouche be at the door , and Aunt Plenty just rustle downstairs in her Sunday best , with Rose like a little black shadow behind her .
Away they drive in state , and all the way Uncle Alec 's hat be more off his head than on , for everyone they meet smile and bow , and give him a blithe a greeting a the day permit .
It be evident that the warning have be a wise one , for , in spite of time and place , the lad be in such a ferment that their elder sit in momentary dread of an unseemly outbreak somewhere .
It be simply impossible to keep those fourteen eye off Uncle Alec , and the dreadful thing that be do during sermon-time will hardly be believe .
Rose dare not look up after a while , for these bad boy vent their emotion upon her till she be ready to laugh and cry with mingled amusement and vexation .
Charlie wink rapturously at her behind his mother 's fan ; Mac openly point to the tall figure beside her ; Jamie star fixedly over the back of his pew , till Rose think his round eye would drop out of his head ; George fell over a stool and drop three book in his excitement ; Will draw sailor and Chinamen on his clean cuff , and display them , to Rose 's great tribulation ; Steve nearly upset the whole party by burn his nose with salt , a he pretend to be overcome by his joy ; even dignify Archie disgrace himself by write in his hymn book , `` Is n't he blue and brown ? ''
and pass it politely to Rose .
Her only salvation be try to fix her attention upon Uncle Mac a portly , placid gentleman , who seem entirely unconscious of the iniquity of the Clan , and doze peacefully in his pew corner .
This be the only uncle Rose have meet for year , for Uncle Jem and Uncle Steve , the husband of Aunt Jessie and Aunt Clara , be at sea , and Aunt Myra be a widow .
Uncle Mac be a merchant , very rich and busy , and as quiet a a mouse at home , for he be in such a minority among the woman folk he dare not open his lip , and let his wife rule undisturbed .
Rose like the big , kindly , silent man who come to her when papa die , be always send her splendid box of goody at school , and often invite her into his great warehouse , full of tea and spice , wine and all sort of foreign fruit , there to eat and carry away whatever she like .
She have secretly regret that he be not to be her guardian ; but since she have see Uncle Alec she felt well about it , for she do not particularly admire Aunt Jane .
When church be over , Dr. Alec get into the porch as quickly a possible , and there the young bear have a hug all round , while the sister shake hand and welcome him with bright face and glad heart .
Rose be nearly crush flat behind a door in that dangerous passage from pew to porch ; but Uncle Mac rescue her , and put her into the carriage for safe keep .
`` Now , girl , I want you to come and dine with Alec ; Mac also , of course .
But I can not ask the boy , for we do not expect this dear fellow till tomorrow , you know , so I make no preparation .
Send the lad home , and let them wait till Monday , for really I be shock at their behaviour in church , '' say Aunt Plenty , a she follow Rose .
In any other place the defraud boy would have set up a howl ; a it be , they growl and protest till Dr. Alec settle the matter by say , `` Never mind , old chap , I 'll make it up to you to-morrow , if you sheer off quietly ; if you do n't , not a blessed thing shall you have out of my big box . ''
Chapter 4 -- Aunts All dinner-time Rose felt that she be go to be talk about , and afterward she be sure of it , for Aunt Plenty whisper to her a they go into the parlour , `` Run up and sit awhile with Sister Peace , my dear .

little Mum !

This chamber have be build out over the library to suit some fancy , and have be unused for year , except at Christmas time , when the old house overflow .
It have three window one to the east , that overlook the bay ; one to the south , where the horse-chestnuts wave their green fan ; and one to the west , towards the hill and the evening sky .
A ruddy sunset burn there now , fill the room with an enchanted glow ; the soft murmur of the sea be hear , and a robin chirp `` Good-night ! ''

Rose saw and hear these thing first , and felt their beauty with a child 's quick instinct ; then her eye take in the altered aspect of the room , once so shrouded , still and solitary , now so full of light and warmth and simple luxury .
India matting cover the floor , with a gay rug here and there ; the antique andiron shine on the wide hearth , where a cheery blaze dispel the dampness of the long-closed room .
Bamboo lounge and chair stand about , and quaint little table in cosy corner ; one bear a pretty basket , one a desk , and on a third lay several familiar-looking book .

Ah !

Chapter 7 -- A Trip to China `` Come , little girl , I 've get another dose for you .
I fancy you wo n't take it as well a you do the last , but you will like it well after a while , '' say Dr. Alec , about a week after the grand surprise .
Rose be sit in her pretty room , where she would gladly have spend all her time if it have be allow ; but she look up with a smile , for she have cease to fear her uncle 's remedy , and be always ready to try a new one .
The last have be a set of light gardening tool , with which she have help him put the flower-beds in order , learn all sort of new and pleasant thing about the plant a she work , for , though she have study botany at school , it seem very dry stuff compare with Uncle Alec 's lively lesson .
`` What be it now ? ''
she ask , shut her work-box without a murmur .
`` Salt-water . ''
`` How must I take it ? ''

`` Yes , sir , '' answer Rose obediently , add to herself , with a shiver , a he go off : `` It be too early for bathing , so I know it be something to do with a dreadful boat . ''
Putting on the new suit of blue flannel , prettily trim with white , and the little sailor-hat with long streamer , divert her mind from the approach trial , till a shrill whistle remind her that her uncle be wait .
Away she run through the garden , down the sandy path , out upon the strip of beach that belong to the house , and here she find Dr. Alec busy with a slender red and white boat that lay rock on the rise tide .
`` That be a dear little boat ; and ` Bonnie Belle ' be a pretty name , '' she say , try not to show how nervous she felt .
`` It be for you ; so sit in the stern and learn to steer , till you be ready to learn to row . ''

she ask , linger a if to tie her hat more firmly .

`` Is it rough to-day ? ''
`` Not very ; it look a trifle squally to the eastward , but we be all right till the wind change .
Come . ''

`` Like a fish .
Now then . ''

Why do you have the stern so far away ? ''
and , stifle several squeak of alarm in her passage , Rose creep to the distant seat , and sit there hold on with both hand and look a if she expect every wave to bring a sudden shipwreck .

Behind them the green Aunt-hill slop gently upward to the grove at the top , and all along the seaward side stand familiar house , stately , cosy , or picturesque .
As they round the Point , the great bay open before them full of shipping , and the city lay beyond , it spire rise above the tall mast with their gay streamer .
`` Are we go there ? ''

`` I 'll show you two genuine Chinamen who have just arrive .
You will like to welcome Whang Lo and Fun See , I 'm sure . ''

That 's the ` Rajah , ' and we will go aboard if we can . ''
In among the ship they go , by the wharf where the water be green and still , and queer barnacle grow on the slippery pile .
Odd smell salute her nose , and odd sight meet her eye , but Rose like it all , and play she be really land in Hong Kong when they glide up to the step in the shadow of the tall `` Rajah . ''
Boxes and bale be rise out of the hold and be carry into the warehouse by stout porter , who tug and bawl and clatter about with small truck , or work crane with iron claw that come down and clutched heavy weight , whisk them aloft to where wide door like mouth swallow them up .
Dr. Alec take her aboard the ship , and she have the satisfaction of poke her inquisitive little nose into every available corner , at the risk of be crush , lose , or drown .
`` Well , child , how would you like to take a voyage round the world with me in a jolly old craft like this ? ''

`` I should like to see the world , but not in such a small , untidy , smelly place a this .
We would go in a yacht all clean and comfortable ; Charlie say that be the proper way , '' answer Rose , survey the close quarter with little favour .
`` You be not a true Campbell if you do n't like the smell of tar and salt-water , nor Charlie either , with his luxurious yacht .
Now come ashore and chin-chin with the Celestials . ''
After a delightful progress through the great warehouse , peep and pick a they go , they find Uncle Mac and the yellow gentleman in his private room , where sample , gift , curiosity , and newly arrive treasure of all sort be pile up in please pro-fusion and con-fusion .
As soon a possible Rose retire to a corner , with a porcelain god on one side , a green dragon on the other , and , what be still more embarrassing , Fun See sit on a tea-chest in front , and star at her with his beady black eye till she do not know where to look .
Mr. Whang Lo be an elderly gentleman in American costume , with his pig-tail neatly wind round his head .
He speak English , and be talk busily with Uncle Mac in the most commonplace way so Rose consider him a failure .
But Fun See be delightfully Chinese from his junk-like shoe to the button on his pagoda hat ; for he have get himself up in style , and be a mass of silk jacket and slouchy trouser .
He be short and fat , and waddle comically ; his eye be very `` slanting , '' a Rose say ; his queue be long , so be his nail ; his yellow face be plump and shiny , and he be altogether a highly satisfactory Chinaman .
Uncle Alec tell her that Fun See have come out to be educate and could only speak a little pigeon English ; so she must be kind to the poor fellow , for he be only a lad , though he look nearly as old a Mr. Whang Lo .
Rose say she would be kind ; but have not the least idea how to entertain the queer guest , who look a if he have walk out of one of the rice-paper landscape on the wall , and sit nod at her so like a toy Mandarin that she could hardly keep sober .
In the midst of her polite perplexity , Uncle Mac saw the two young people gaze wistfully at one another , and seem to enjoy the joke of this make acquaintance under difficulty .
Taking a box from his table , he give it to Fun See , with an order that seem to please him very much .
Descending from his perch , he fell to unpack it with great neatness and despatch , while Rose watch him , wonder what be go to happen .
Presently , out from the wrapping come a teapot , which cause her to clasp her hand with delight , for it be make in the likeness of a plump little Chinaman .
His hat be the cover , his queue the handle , and his pipe the nose .
It stand upon foot in shoe turn up at the toe , and the smile on the fat , sleepy face be so like that on Fun 's when he display the teapot , that Rose could n't help laughing , which please him much .
Two pretty cup with cover , and a fine scarlet tray complete the set , and make one long to have a `` dish of tea , '' even in Chinese style , without cream or sugar .
When he have arrange them on a little table before her , Fun signify in pantomime that they be hers , from her uncle .
She return her thanks in the same way , whereupon he return to his tea-chest , and , have no other mean of communication , they sit smile and nod at one another in an absurd sort of way till a new idea seem to strike Fun .
Tumbling off his seat , he waddle away as fast a his petticoat permit , leave Rose hop that he have not go to get a roasted rat , a stewed puppy , or any other foreign mess which civility would oblige her to eat .
While she wait for her funny new friend , she improve her mind in a way that would have charm Aunt Jane .
The gentleman be talk over all sort of thing , and she listen attentively , store up much of what she hear , for she have an excellent memory , and long to distinguish herself by be able to produce some useful information when reproached with her ignorance .
She be just try to impress upon her mind that Amoy be two hundred and eighty mile from Hong Kong , when Fun come scuffle back , bear what she think be a small sword , till he unfurl an immense fan , and present it with a string of Chinese compliment , the meaning of which would have amuse her even more than the sound , if she could have understand it .
She have never see such an astonishing fan , and at once become absorb in examine it .
Of course , there be no perspective whatever , which only give it a peculiar charm to Rose , for in one place a lovely lady , with blue knitting-needles in her hair , sit directly upon the spire of a stately pagoda .
In another charm view a brook appear to flow in at the front door of a stout gentleman 's house , and out at his chimney .
In a third a zig-zag wall go up into the sky like a flash of lightning , and a bird with two tail be apparently brood over a fisherman whose boat be just go aground upon the moon .
It be altogether a fascinating thing , and she would have sit waft it to and fro all the afternoon , to Fun 's great satisfaction , if Dr. Alec 's attention have not suddenly be call to her by a breeze from the big fan that blow his hair into his eye , and remind him that they must go .
So the pretty china be repacked , Rose furl her fan , and with several parcel of choice tea for the old lady stow away in Dr. Alec 's pocket , they take their leave , after Fun have salute them with `` the three bending and the nine knocking , '' a they salute the Emperor , or `` Son of Heaven , '' at home .
`` I feel a if I have really be to China , and I 'm sure I look so , '' say Rose , a they glide out of the shadow of the `` Rajah . ''
She certainly do , for Mr. Whang Lo have give her a Chinese umbrella ; Uncle Alec have get some lantern to light up her balcony ; the great fan lay in her lap , and the tea-set repose at her foot .
`` This be not a bad way to study geography , be it ? ''
ask her uncle , who have observe her attention to the talk .
`` It be a very pleasant way , and I really think I have learn more about China to-day than in all the lesson I have at school , though I use to rattle off the answer a fast a I could go .
No one explain anything to u , so all I remember be that tea and silk come from there , and the woman have little bit of foot .
I saw Fun look at mine , and he must have think them perfectly immense , '' answer Rose , survey her stout boot with sudden contempt .
`` We will have out the map and the globe , and I 'll show you some of my journey , tell story a we go .
That will be next best to do it actually . ''
`` You be so fond of travel , I should think it would be very dull for you here , uncle .
Do you know , Aunt Plenty say she be sure you will be off in a year or two . ''
`` Very likely . ''
`` Oh , me !
what shall I do then ? ''
sigh Rose , in a tone of despair that make Uncle Alec 's face brighten with a look of genuine pleasure a he say significantly , `` Next time I go I shall take my little anchor with me .
How will that suit ? ''
`` Really , uncle ? ''
`` Really , niece . ''
Rose give a little bounce of rapture which cause the boat to `` wiggle '' in a way that speedily quiet her down .
But she sit beam joyfully and try to think which of some hundred question she would ask first , when Dr. Alec say , point to a boat that be come up behind them in great style , `` How well those fellow row !
Look at them , and take note for your own use by and by . ''
The `` Stormy Petrel '' be man by half a dozen jaunty look sailor , who make a fine display of blue shirt and shiny hat , with star and anchor in every direction .
`` How beautifully they go , and they be only boy .
Why , I do believe they be our boy !
Yes , I see Charlie laugh over his shoulder .
Row , uncle , row !
Oh , please do , and not let them catch up with u ! ''
cry Rose , in such a state of excitement that the new umbrella nearly go overboard .
`` All right , here we go ! ''
and away they do go with a long steady sweep of the oar that carry the `` Bonnie Belle '' through the water with a rush .
The lad pull their prettiest , but Dr. Alec would have reach the Point first , if Rose , in her flurry , have not retard him by jerk the rudder rope in a most unseamanlike way , and just a she get right again her hat blow off .
That put an end to the race , and while they be still fish for the hat the other boat come alongside , with all the oar in the air , and the jolly young tar ready for a frolic .
`` Did you catch a crab , uncle ? ''
`` No , a blue-fish , '' he answer , a the drip hat be land on a seat to dry .
`` What have you be do ? ''
`` Seeing Fun . ''
`` Good for you , Rose !
I know what you mean .
We be go to have him up to show u how to fly the big kite , for we ca n't get the hang of it .
Is n't he great fun , though ? ''
`` No , little Fun . ''
`` Come , stop joking , and show u what you 've get . ''
`` You 'd better hoist that fan for a sail . ''
`` Lend Dandy your umbrella ; he hat to burn his pretty nose . ''
`` I say , uncle , be you go to have a Feast of Lanterns ? ''
`` No , I 'm go to have a feast of bread and butter , for it 's tea-time .
If that black cloud do n't lie , we shall have a gust before long , so you have good get home as soon a you can , or your mother will be anxious , Archie . ''
`` Ay , ay , skipper .
Good-night , Rose ; come out often , and we 'll teach you all there be to know about rowing , '' be Charlie 's modest invitation .
Then the boat part company , and across the water from the `` Petrel 's '' crew come a verse from one of the Nonsense song in which the boy delight .
`` Oh , Timballoo !
how happy we be , We live in a sieve and a crockery jar !
And all night long , in the starlight pale , We sail away , with a pea-green sail , And whistle and warble a moony song To the echo sound of a coppery gong .
Far and few , far and few Are the land where the Jumblies live ; Their head be green , and their hand be blue , And they go to sea in a sieve . ''
Chapter 8 -- And what come of it `` Uncle , could you lend me a ninepence ?
I 'll return it as soon a I get my pocket-money , '' say Rose , come into the library in a great hurry that even .

`` If the sacrifice be a true one .

`` Yes . ''

`` Yes . ''

`` I 'll go good night ! ''
and throw him a kiss , the little ghost vanish , leave Uncle Alec to pace the shore and think about some of the unsuspected sacrifice that have make him what he be .
Chapter 10 -- Rose 's Sacrifice There certainly be `` lark '' on Campbell 's Island next day , a Charlie have foretell , and Rose take her part in them like one intent on enjoy every minute to the utmost .

Chapter 11 -- Poor Mac Rose 's sacrifice be a failure in one respect , for , though the elder love her the good for it , and show that they do , the boy be not inspire with the sudden respect which she have hop for .

Chapter 12 -- `` The Other Fellows '' Rose do tell `` the people '' what have pass , and no one `` howl '' over Mac , or say a word to trouble him .
He have his talk with the doctor , and get very little comfort out of it , for he find that `` just what he might do '' be nothing at all ; though the prospect of some study by and by , if all go well , give him courage to bear the woe of the present .
Having make up his mind to this , he behave so well that everyone be astonish , never have suspect so much manliness in the quiet Worm .
The boy be much impress , both by the greatness of the affliction which hung over him and by his way of bear it .
They be very good to him , but not always particularly wise in their attempt to cheer and amuse ; and Rose often find him much downcast after a visit of condolence from the Clan .
She still keep her place a head-nurse and chief-reader , though the boy do their best in an irregular sort of way .
They be rather take aback sometimes at find Rose 's service prefer to their 's , and privately confide to one another that `` Old Mac be get fond of be molly-coddled . ''
But they could not help see how useful she be , and own that she alone have remain faithful a fact which cause some of them much secret compunction now and then .
Rose felt that she rule in that room , if nowhere else , for Aunt Jane leave a great deal to her , find that her experience with her invalid father fit her for a nurse , and in a case like this , her youth be an advantage rather than a drawback .
Mac soon come to think that no one could take care of him so well a Rose , and Rose soon grow fond of her patient , though at first she have consider this cousin the least attractive of the seven .
He be not polite and sensible like Archie , nor gay and handsome like Prince Charlie , nor neat and oblige like Steve , nor amuse like the `` Brats , '' nor confide and affectionate like little Jamie .
He be rough , absent-minded , careless , and awkward , rather priggish , and not at all agreeable to a dainty , beauty-loving girl like Rose .

Chapter 13 -- Cosey Corner Vacation be over , the boy go back to school , and poor Mac be leave lamenting .
